n.i.e.</td>\n<td>2,760</td>\n<td><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">6999400000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>0.4%\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#efefef; font-weight:bold">\n<td colspan="2">Total population</td>\n<td>690,005</td>\n<td><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7002100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>100%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_corporations_based_in_Winnipeg" title="List of corporations based in Winnipeg">List of corporations based in Winnipeg</a></div>\n<p>Winnipeg is an economic base and regional centre. It has one of the country\'s most diversified economies,<sup id="cite_ref-edw_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edw-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> with major employment in the trade (15.2%), manufacturing (9.8%), educational (7.7%), and health care and social assistance (15.2%) sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-edw_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edw-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> There were approximately 21,000 employers in the city as of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-edw_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edw-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnipeg_Mint.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Winnipeg_Mint.JPG/220px-Winnipeg_Mint.JPG" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Winnipeg_Mint.JPG/330px-Winnipeg_Mint.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Winnipeg_Mint.JPG/440px-Winnipeg_Mint.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnipeg_Mint.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Mint" title="Royal Canadian Mint">Royal Canadian Mint</a>\'s facility in Winnipeg produces <a href="/wiki/Coins_of_the_Canadian_dollar" title="Coins of the Canadian dollar">Canadian coins</a> for circulation, as well as foreign coins.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2013, The CIBC Metropolitan Economic Activity Index rated Winnipeg\'s economy as fourth in a national survey of 25 city economies, behind Toronto, Calgary, and Regina.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> According to the Conference Board of Canada, Winnipeg was projected to experience a real GDP growth of 2 percent in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Unlike most of Canada, the city experienced a decrease in unemployment in 2013, ending the year at a rate of 5.8 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> As of 2010, median household income in the city was $72,050.<sup id="cite_ref-edw_114-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edw-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  January&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, approximately 416,700 people are employed in Winnipeg and the surrounding area.<sup id="cite_ref-Statistcs_Canada_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistcs_Canada-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Some of Winnipeg\'s largest employers are government and government-funded institutions, including the Province of Manitoba, the City of Winnipeg, the University of Manitoba, the <a href="/wiki/Health_Sciences_Centre_(Winnipeg)" title="Health Sciences Centre (Winnipeg)">Health Sciences Centre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Hydro" title="Manitoba Hydro">Manitoba Hydro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Approximately 54,000 people (14% of the work force) are employed in the public sector as of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-employ_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-employ-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Large private sector employers include <a href="/wiki/Shaw_Communications" title="Shaw Communications">Shaw Communications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Telecom_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Manitoba Telecom Services">Manitoba Telecom Services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ipsos-Reid" title="Ipsos-Reid">Ipsos-Reid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palliser_Furniture" title="Palliser Furniture">Palliser Furniture</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Great-West_Life_Assurance_Company" title="The Great-West Life Assurance Company">Great-West Life Assurance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motor_Coach_Industries" title="Motor Coach Industries">Motor Coach Industries</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Flyer_Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="New Flyer Industries">New Flyer Industries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Canada_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing Canada Technology">Boeing Canada Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Standard_Aero_Corporation_(c.1911)" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Aero Corporation (c.1911)">StandardAero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magellan_Aerospace" title="Magellan Aerospace">Magellan Aerospace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nyg%C3%A5rd_International" title="Nyg\xc3\xa5rd International">Nyg\xc3\xa5rd International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canad_Inns" title="Canad Inns">Canad Inns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada_Goose_(clothing)" title="Canada Goose (clothing)">Canada Goose clothing</a> and <a href="/wiki/IGM_Financial" title="IGM Financial">Investors Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Mint" title="Royal Canadian Mint">Royal Canadian Mint</a>, established in 1976, produces all circulating coinage in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The plant, in southeastern Winnipeg, also produces coins for many other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, Winnipeg was ranked by <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a> as the least expensive location to do business in western Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Like many prairie cities, Winnipeg has a relatively low cost of living.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> According to the Canadian Real Estate Association, the average house price in Winnipeg was $260,000 as of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> As of May 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Price_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumer Price Index">Consumer Price Index</a> was 125.8 relative to 2002 prices, reflecting consumer costs at the Canadian average.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_arts_and_culture" title="Winnipeg arts and culture">Winnipeg arts and culture</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Winnipeg" title="List of people from Winnipeg">List of people from Winnipeg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Museums_in_Winnipeg" title="Category:Museums in Winnipeg">Category:Museums in Winnipeg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Theatre_companies_in_Manitoba" title="Category:Theatre companies in Manitoba">Category:Theatre companies in Manitoba</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_TV_and_films_shot_in_Winnipeg" title="List of TV and films shot in Winnipeg">List of TV and films shot in Winnipeg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Winnipeg_musicians" title="List of Winnipeg musicians">List of Winnipeg musicians</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Esplanderiel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Esplanderiel.jpg/220px-Esplanderiel.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Esplanderiel.jpg/330px-Esplanderiel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Esplanderiel.jpg/440px-Esplanderiel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="696" data-file-height="928" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Esplanderiel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Esplanade_Riel" title="Esplanade Riel">Esplanade Riel</a> is a landmark and pedestrian bridge in the city. It connects downtown Winnipeg with the <a href="/wiki/St._Boniface,_Winnipeg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Boniface, Winnipeg">St. Boniface</a> neighbourhood.</div></div></div>\n<p>Winnipeg was named the Cultural Capital of Canada in 2010 by Canadian Heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> As of 2012, there are 26 <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Historic_Sites_of_Canada_in_Manitoba" title="List of National Historic Sites of Canada in Manitoba">National Historic Sites of Canada</a> in Winnipeg.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> One of these, <a href="/wiki/The_Forks,_Winnipeg" title="The Forks, Winnipeg">The Forks</a>, attracts four million visitors a year.<sup id="cite_ref-forks_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forks-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> It is home to the <a href="/wiki/City_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="City (TV network)">City</a> television studio, <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Theatre_for_Young_People" title="Manitoba Theatre for Young People">Manitoba Theatre for Young People</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_International_Children%27s_Festival" title="Winnipeg International Children&#39;s Festival">Winnipeg International Children\'s Festival</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Children%27s_Museum" title="Manitoba Children&#39;s Museum">Manitoba Children\'s Museum</a>. It also features a 30,000-square-foot (2,800&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) skate plaza, a 8,500-square-foot (790&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) bowl complex, the <a href="/wiki/Esplanade_Riel" title="Esplanade Riel">Esplanade Riel</a> bridge,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> a river walkway, <a href="/wiki/Shaw_Park" title="Shaw Park">Shaw Park</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights" title="Canadian Museum for Human Rights">Canadian Museum for Human Rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-forks_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forks-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Public_Library" title="Winnipeg Public Library">Winnipeg Public Library</a> is a public library network with 20 branches throughout the city, including the main <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Library_(Winnipeg)" title="Millennium Library (Winnipeg)">Millennium Library</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_the_Bear" class="mw-redirect" title="Winnipeg the Bear">Winnipeg the Bear</a>, which would become the inspiration for part of the name of <a href="/wiki/Winnie-the-Pooh" title="Winnie-the-Pooh">Winnie-the-Pooh</a>, was purchased in Ontario by Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Harry_Colebourn" title="Harry Colebourn">Harry Colebourn</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Fort_Garry_Horse" title="The Fort Garry Horse">the Fort Garry Horse</a>. He named the bear after the regiment\'s home town of Winnipeg.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._A._Milne" title="A. A. Milne">A. A. Milne</a> later wrote a series of books featuring the fictional Winnie-the-Pooh. The series\' illustrator, <a href="/wiki/E._H._Shepard" title="E. H. Shepard">Ernest H. Shepard</a>, created the only known oil painting of Winnipeg\'s adopted fictional bear, displayed in Assiniboine Park.<sup id="cite_ref-shepard_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shepard-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city has developed many distinct dishes and cooking styles, notably in the areas of <a href="/wiki/Confectionery" title="Confectionery">confectionery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hot-smoking" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot-smoking">hot-smoked fish</a>. Both the First Nations and more recent Eastern Canadian, European, and Asian immigrants have helped shape Winnipeg\'s dining scene, giving birth to dishes such as the desserts <a href="/wiki/Schmoo_torte" title="Schmoo torte">schmoo torte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flapper_pie" title="Flapper pie">wafer pie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Art_Gallery" title="Winnipeg Art Gallery">Winnipeg Art Gallery</a> is Western Canada\'s oldest public art gallery, founded in 1912. It is the sixth-largest in the country<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> and includes the world\'s largest public collection of contemporary Inuit art.<sup id="cite_ref-ce_17-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ce-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Since the late 1970s Winnipeg has also had an active <a href="/wiki/Canadian_artist-run_centres" title="Canadian artist-run centres">artist run centre</a> culture.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centennial_Concert_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Centennial_Concert_Hall.jpg/220px-Centennial_Concert_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Centennial_Concert_Hall.jpg/330px-Centennial_Concert_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Centennial_Concert_Hall.jpg/440px-Centennial_Concert_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centennial_Concert_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Centennial_Concert_Hall" title="Centennial Concert Hall">Centennial Concert Hall</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Performing arts centre">performing arts centre</a> and is home to the <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Opera" title="Manitoba Opera">Manitoba Opera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Winnipeg_Ballet" title="Royal Winnipeg Ballet">Royal Winnipeg Ballet</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Winnipeg Symphony Orchestra">Winnipeg Symphony Orchestra</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Winnipeg\'s three largest performing arts venues, the <a href="/wiki/Centennial_Concert_Hall" title="Centennial Concert Hall">Centennial Concert Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Manitoba_Theatre_Centre" title="Royal Manitoba Theatre Centre">Royal Manitoba Theatre Centre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pantages_Playhouse_Theatre" title="Pantages Playhouse Theatre">Pantages Playhouse Theatre</a>, are downtown. The Royal Manitoba is Canada\'s oldest English-language regional theatre, with over 250 performances yearly.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The Pantages Playhouse Theatre opened as a <a href="/wiki/Vaudeville#Architecture" title="Vaudeville">vaudeville house</a> in 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Other city theatres include the <a href="/wiki/Burton_Cummings_Theatre" title="Burton Cummings Theatre">Burton Cummings Theatre</a> (a National Historic Site of Canada built in 1906<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>) and <a href="/wiki/Prairie_Theatre_Exchange" title="Prairie Theatre Exchange">Prairie Theatre Exchange</a>. <a href="/wiki/Le_Cercle_Moli%C3%A8re" title="Le Cercle Moli\xc3\xa8re">Le Cercle Moli\xc3\xa8re</a>, based in St Boniface, is Canada\'s oldest theatre company; it was founded in 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Stage" title="Rainbow Stage">Rainbow Stage</a> is a musical theatre production company based in <a href="/wiki/Kildonan_Park" title="Kildonan Park">Kildonan Park</a> that produces professional, live Broadway musical shows and is Canada\'s longest-surviving outdoor theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-ce_17-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ce-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Theatre_for_Young_People" title="Manitoba Theatre for Young People">Manitoba Theatre for Young People</a> at The Forks is one of only two Theatres for Young Audiences in Canada with a permanent residence and the only Theatre for Young Audiences that offers a full season of plays for teenagers.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Jewish_Theatre" title="Winnipeg Jewish Theatre">Winnipeg Jewish Theatre</a> is the only professional theatre in Canada dedicated to Jewish themes.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare_in_the_Ruins" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare in the Ruins">Shakespeare in the Ruins</a> (SIR) presents adaptations of <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a> plays.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winnipeg has hosted a number of <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">Hollywood</a> productions: <i><a href="/wiki/Shall_We_Dance%3F_(2004_film)" title="Shall We Dance? (2004 film)">Shall We Dance?</a></i> (2004), <i><a href="/wiki/Capote_(film)" title="Capote (film)">Capote</a></i> (2005), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Assassination_of_Jesse_James_by_the_Coward_Robert_Ford" title="The Assassination of Jesse James by the Coward Robert Ford">The Assassination of Jesse James by the Coward Robert Ford</a></i> (2007), and <i><a href="/wiki/Goon_(film)" title="Goon (film)">Goon</a></i> (2011) among others had parts filmed in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Film_Group" title="Winnipeg Film Group">Winnipeg Film Group</a> has produced numerous award-winning films.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> There are several TV and film production companies in Winnipeg: the most prominent are <a href="/wiki/Farpoint_Films" title="Farpoint Films">Farpoint Films</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frantic_Films" title="Frantic Films">Frantic Films</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Gal_Pictures" title="Buffalo Gal Pictures">Buffalo Gal Pictures</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Les_Productions_Rivard" title="Les Productions Rivard">Les Productions Rivard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Guy Maddin\'s <i><a href="/wiki/My_Winnipeg" title="My Winnipeg">My Winnipeg</a></i>, an independent film released in 2008, is a comedic rumination on the city\'s history.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights_as_seen_from_The_Forks_Tower_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/The_Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights_as_seen_from_The_Forks_Tower_02.JPG/220px-The_Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights_as_seen_from_The_Forks_Tower_02.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/The_Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights_as_seen_from_The_Forks_Tower_02.JPG/330px-The_Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights_as_seen_from_The_Forks_Tower_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/The_Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights_as_seen_from_The_Forks_Tower_02.JPG/440px-The_Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights_as_seen_from_The_Forks_Tower_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2296" data-file-height="1723" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights_as_seen_from_The_Forks_Tower_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Located in Winnipeg, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights" title="Canadian Museum for Human Rights">Canadian Museum for Human Rights</a> is a <a href="/wiki/National_museums_of_Canada" title="National museums of Canada">national museums of Canada</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Winnipeg Symphony Orchestra">Winnipeg Symphony Orchestra</a> is the largest and oldest professional musical ensemble in Winnipeg.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Chamber_Orchestra" title="Manitoba Chamber Orchestra">Manitoba Chamber Orchestra</a> runs a series of chamber orchestral concerts each year.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Opera" title="Manitoba Opera">Manitoba Opera</a> is Manitoba\'s only full-time professional opera company.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Among the most notable musical acts associated with Winnipeg are <a href="/wiki/Comeback_Kid_(band)" title="Comeback Kid (band)">Comeback Kid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bachman%E2%80%93Turner_Overdrive" title="Bachman\xe2\x80\x93Turner Overdrive">Bachman\xe2\x80\x93Turner Overdrive</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-juno_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-juno-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Crash_Test_Dummies" title="Crash Test Dummies">Crash Test Dummies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Guess_Who" title="The Guess Who">The Guess Who</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neil_Young" title="Neil Young">Neil Young</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Wailin%27_Jennys" title="The Wailin&#39; Jennys">The Wailin\' Jennys</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Weakerthans" title="The Weakerthans">The Weakerthans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-juno_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-juno-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Winnipeg_Ballet" title="Royal Winnipeg Ballet">Royal Winnipeg Ballet</a> (RWB) is Canada\'s oldest <a href="/wiki/Ballet_company" title="Ballet company">ballet company</a> and the longest continuously operating ballet company in North America. It was the first organization to be granted a <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal title</a> by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, and has included notable dancers such as <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Hart" title="Evelyn Hart">Evelyn Hart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Baryshnikov" title="Mikhail Baryshnikov">Mikhail Baryshnikov</a>. The RWB also runs a full-time classical dance school.<sup id="cite_ref-rwb_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rwb-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Museum" title="Manitoba Museum">Manitoba Museum</a>, the city\'s largest museum, depicts the history of the city and province. The full-size replica of the ship <a href="/wiki/Nonsuch_(1650_ship)" title="Nonsuch (1650 ship)"><i>Nonsuch</i></a> is the museum\'s showcase piece.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Children%27s_Museum" title="Manitoba Children&#39;s Museum">Manitoba Children\'s Museum</a> is a nonprofit <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_museum" title="Children&#39;s museum">children\'s museum</a> at The Forks that features twelve permanent galleries.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Museum_for_Human_Rights" title="Canadian Museum for Human Rights">Canadian Museum for Human Rights</a> is the second Canadian <a href="/wiki/National_museum" class="mw-redirect" title="National museum">national museum</a> for human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The federal government has contributed $100 million towards the estimated $311-million project.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Construction of the museum began on 1 April 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> and the museum opened to the public 27 September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Western_Canada_Aviation_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Canada Aviation Museum">Western Canada Aviation Museum</a>, in a hangar at Winnipeg\'s <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_James_Armstrong_Richardson_International_Airport" title="Winnipeg James Armstrong Richardson International Airport">James Richardson International Airport</a>, features military jets, commercial aircraft, Canada\'s first helicopter, the "flying saucer" <a href="/wiki/Avrocar" class="mw-redirect" title="Avrocar">Avrocar</a>, flight simulators, and a <a href="/wiki/Black_Brant_(rocket)" title="Black Brant (rocket)">Black Brant</a> rocket built in Manitoba by <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Aerospace" title="Bristol Aerospace">Bristol Aerospace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McCaffery2000_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCaffery2000-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Railway_Museum" title="Winnipeg Railway Museum">Winnipeg Railway Museum</a> at Via Rail Station has a variety of locomotives, notably the <i><a href="/wiki/Countess_of_Dufferin" title="Countess of Dufferin">Countess of Dufferin</a></i>, the first <a href="/wiki/Steam_locomotive" title="Steam locomotive">steam locomotive</a> in Western Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Winnipeg_Railway_Museum_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Winnipeg_Railway_Museum-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Festivals_in_Winnipeg" title="Category:Festivals in Winnipeg">Category:Festivals in Winnipeg</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Korean_Pavilion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Korean_Pavilion.jpg/220px-Korean_Pavilion.jpg" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Korean_Pavilion.jpg/330px-Korean_Pavilion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Korean_Pavilion.jpg/440px-Korean_Pavilion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5471" data-file-height="2389" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Korean_Pavilion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Korean Pavilion during <a href="/wiki/Folklorama" title="Folklorama">Folklorama</a>. It claims to be the largest and longest-running cultural festival in the world.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Festival_du_Voyageur" title="Festival du Voyageur">Festival du Voyageur</a>, Western Canada\'s largest winter festival, celebrates the early French explorers of the Red River Valley.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Folklorama" title="Folklorama">Folklorama</a> is the largest and longest-running cultural celebration festival in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-folklorama1_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-folklorama1-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jazz_Winnipeg_Festival" title="Jazz Winnipeg Festival">Jazz Winnipeg Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Folk_Festival" title="Winnipeg Folk Festival">Winnipeg Folk Festival</a> both celebrate Winnipeg\'s music community. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg_Music_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Winnipeg Music Festival (page does not exist)">Winnipeg Music Festival</a> offers a competition venue to amateur musicians. The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Fringe_Theatre_Festival" title="Winnipeg Fringe Theatre Festival">Winnipeg Fringe Theatre Festival</a> is the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Alternative_theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative theatre">alternative theatre</a> festival in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_International_Writers_Festival" title="Winnipeg International Writers Festival">Winnipeg International Writers Festival</a> (also called THIN AIR) brings writers to Winnipeg for workshops and readings.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> community in the city is served by <a href="/wiki/Pride_Winnipeg" title="Pride Winnipeg">Pride Winnipeg</a>, an annual <a href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">gay pride</a> festival and parade, and <a href="/wiki/Reel_Pride" title="Reel Pride">Reel Pride</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Film_festival" title="Film festival">film festival</a> of LGBT-themed films.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Winnipeg" title="Sport in Winnipeg">Sport in Winnipeg</a></div>\n<p>Winnipeg has been home to several professional <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">hockey</a> teams. The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Jets" title="Winnipeg Jets">Winnipeg Jets</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a> (NHL) have called the city home since 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The original <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Jets_(1972-96)" class="mw-redirect" title="Winnipeg Jets (1972-96)">Winnipeg Jets</a>, the city\'s former NHL team, left for <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a> after the 1995\xe2\x80\x9396 season due to mounting financial troubles, despite a campaign effort to "Save the Jets".<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The Jets play at <a href="/wiki/Bell_MTS_Place" title="Bell MTS Place">Bell MTS Place</a>, which is ranked the world\'s 19th-busiest arena among non-sporting touring events, 13th-busiest among facilities in North America, and 3rd-busiest in Canada as of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MTS_CENTRE_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/MTS_CENTRE_b.jpg/220px-MTS_CENTRE_b.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/MTS_CENTRE_b.jpg/330px-MTS_CENTRE_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/MTS_CENTRE_b.jpg/440px-MTS_CENTRE_b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1015" data-file-height="535" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MTS_CENTRE_b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bell_MTS_Place" title="Bell MTS Place">Bell MTS Place</a> is an indoor arena in downtown Winnipeg. It is the home arena of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Jets" title="Winnipeg Jets">Winnipeg Jets</a> and the <a href="/wiki/American_Hockey_League" title="American Hockey League">AHL</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Moose" title="Manitoba Moose">Manitoba Moose</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Past hockey teams based in Winnipeg include the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Maroons" title="Winnipeg Maroons">Winnipeg Maroons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Warriors" title="Winnipeg Warriors">Winnipeg Warriors</a>, three time Stanley Cup Champion <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Victorias" title="Winnipeg Victorias">Winnipeg Victorias</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Falcons" title="Winnipeg Falcons">Winnipeg Falcons</a>, who were the first ever Gold Medal Olympians, representing Canada in 1920 in Antwerp, Belgium. Another professional ice hockey team in Winnipeg is the <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Moose" title="Manitoba Moose">Manitoba Moose</a>, the American Hockey League primary affiliate of the Winnipeg Jets that are owned by the same group .<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In amateur hockey, the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Blues" title="Winnipeg Blues">Winnipeg Blues</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Junior_Hockey_League" title="Manitoba Junior Hockey League">Manitoba Junior Hockey League</a> play out of the <a href="/wiki/Bell_MTS_Iceplex" title="Bell MTS Iceplex">Bell MTS Iceplex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> On the international stage, Winnipeg has hosted national and world hockey championships on a number of occasions, most notably the <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Junior_Ice_Hockey_Championships" title="1999 World Junior Ice Hockey Championships">1999 World Junior Hockey Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_IIHF_Women%27s_World_Championship" title="2007 IIHF Women&#39;s World Championship">2007 Women\'s World Hockey Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Blue_Bombers" title="Winnipeg Blue Bombers">Winnipeg Blue Bombers</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">Canadian Football League</a>. They are ten-time <a href="/wiki/Grey_Cup" title="Grey Cup">Grey Cup</a> champions, their last championship in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-gc_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gc-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> From 1953 to 2012, the Blue Bombers called <a href="/wiki/Canad_Inns_Stadium" title="Canad Inns Stadium">Canad Inns Stadium</a> home; they have since moved to <a href="/wiki/Investors_Group_Field" title="Investors Group Field">Investors Group Field</a>. Due to construction delays and cost overruns, the stadium was not ready for the 2012 CFL season, instead opening in 2013. The $200-million facility is also the home to the <a href="/wiki/CIS_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="CIS Football">CIS\'</a> University of Manitoba Bisons and the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Rifles" title="Winnipeg Rifles">Winnipeg Rifles</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Junior_Football_League" title="Canadian Junior Football League">Canadian Junior Football League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Investors_Group_CANnwt_vs_USnwt.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Investors_Group_CANnwt_vs_USnwt.png/220px-Investors_Group_CANnwt_vs_USnwt.png" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Investors_Group_CANnwt_vs_USnwt.png/330px-Investors_Group_CANnwt_vs_USnwt.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Investors_Group_CANnwt_vs_USnwt.png/440px-Investors_Group_CANnwt_vs_USnwt.png 2x" data-file-width="1239" data-file-height="925" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Investors_Group_CANnwt_vs_USnwt.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Investors_Group_Field" title="Investors Group Field">Investors Group Field</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Multi-purpose_stadium" title="Multi-purpose stadium">multi-purpose stadium</a> in the city. The stadium is also the home stadium for the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">CFL</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Blue_Bombers" title="Winnipeg Blue Bombers">Winnipeg Blue Bombers</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The University of <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Bisons" title="Manitoba Bisons">Manitoba Bisons</a> and the University of <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Wesmen" title="Winnipeg Wesmen">Winnipeg Wesmen</a> represent the city in <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">interuniversity sport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> In soccer, it is represented by <a href="/wiki/WSA_Winnipeg" title="WSA Winnipeg">WSA Winnipeg</a> in the <a href="/wiki/USL_Premier_Development_League" class="mw-redirect" title="USL Premier Development League">USL Premier Development League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Winnipeg will have a team in the new <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Premier_League" title="Canadian Premier League">Canadian Premier League</a> for the inaugural season in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winnipeg has been home to a number of professional baseball teams, most recently the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Goldeyes" title="Winnipeg Goldeyes">Winnipeg Goldeyes</a> since 1994. The Goldeyes play at <a href="/wiki/Shaw_Park" title="Shaw Park">Shaw Park</a>, which was completed in 1999. The team had led the <a href="/wiki/Northern_League_(baseball,_1993%E2%80%932010)" title="Northern League (baseball, 1993\xe2\x80\x932010)">Northern League</a> for ten straight years in average attendance through 2010, with more than 300,000 annual fan visits, until the league collapsed and merged into the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_of_Independent_Professional_Baseball" title="American Association of Independent Professional Baseball">American Association of Independent Professional Baseball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winnipeg was the first Canadian city to host the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a>, and the second city to host the event twice, in <a href="/wiki/1967_Pan_American_Games" title="1967 Pan American Games">1967</a> and again in <a href="/wiki/1999_Pan_American_Games" title="1999 Pan American Games">1999</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Pool" title="Pan Am Pool">Pan Am Pool</a>, built for the 1967 Pan Am Games, hosts aquatic events, including <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">diving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">speed swimming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synchronized_swimming" class="mw-redirect" title="Synchronized swimming">synchronized swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-indoor_pools_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indoor_pools-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Winnipeg co-hosted the <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2015 FIFA Women&#39;s World Cup">2015 FIFA Women\'s World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> The city has been selected to host the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Canada_Summer_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="Canada Summer Games">Canada Summer Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> Winnipeg will host the <a href="/wiki/World_Police_and_Fire_Games" title="World Police and Fire Games">World Police and Fire Games</a> in 2023.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Professional sports teams\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Club\n</th>\n<th>Sport\n</th>\n<th>League\n</th>\n<th>Venue\n</th>\n<th>Established\n</th>\n<th>Championships\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a
