Hockey">Ice Hockey</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/International_Hockey_League_(1945%E2%80%932001)" title="International Hockey League (1945\xe2\x80\x932001)">IHL</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Hockey_League" title="American Hockey League">AHL</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Arena" title="Winnipeg Arena">Winnipeg Arena</a> (1996\xe2\x80\x932004)<br /><a href="/wiki/Bell_MTS_Place" title="Bell MTS Place">Bell MTS Place</a> (2004\xe2\x80\x932011, 2015\xe2\x80\x93present)\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1996\xe2\x80\x932011, 2015\xe2\x80\x93present\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">0\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_media">Local media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Local media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CTV_Winnipeg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/CTV_Winnipeg.jpg/220px-CTV_Winnipeg.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/CTV_Winnipeg.jpg/330px-CTV_Winnipeg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/CTV_Winnipeg.jpg/440px-CTV_Winnipeg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1932" data-file-height="1542" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CTV_Winnipeg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/CKY-DT" title="CKY-DT">CTV Winnipeg</a> is one of five English-language television broadcasters in Winnipeg.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Winnipeg" title="Media in Winnipeg">Media in Winnipeg</a></div>\n<p>Winnipeg has two daily newspapers: the <i><a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Free_Press" title="Winnipeg Free Press">Winnipeg Free Press</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Sun" title="Winnipeg Sun">Winnipeg Sun</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> There are five weekly newspapers delivered free to most Winnipeg households by region. There are also several ethnic weekly newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Local magazines include <i><a href="/wiki/Border_Crossings_(magazine)" title="Border Crossings (magazine)">Border Crossings</a></i>.\n</p><p>Television broadcasting in Winnipeg started in 1954. The federal government refused to license any private broadcaster until the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Canadian Broadcasting Corporation">Canadian Broadcasting Corporation</a> had created a national network. In May 1954, <a href="/wiki/CBWT" class="mw-redirect" title="CBWT">CBWT</a> went on the air with four hours of broadcasting per day.<sup id="cite_ref-A_History_v_1995_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_History_v_1995-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> There are now five English-language stations and one French-language station based in Winnipeg. Additionally, some American network affiliates are available over-the-air.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Winnipeg is home to 33 AM and FM radio stations, two of which are <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French-language</a> stations.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CBC_Radio_One" title="CBC Radio One">CBC Radio One</a> and <a href="/wiki/CBC_Radio_2" class="mw-redirect" title="CBC Radio 2">CBC Radio 2</a> broadcast local and national programming in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Native_Communications_Inc" class="mw-redirect" title="Native Communications Inc">NCI</a> is devoted to Aboriginal programming.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Law and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law,_government,_and_crime_in_Winnipeg" title="Law, government, and crime in Winnipeg">Law, government, and crime in Winnipeg</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnipeg%27s_City_Hall_building.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Winnipeg%27s_City_Hall_building.JPG/220px-Winnipeg%27s_City_Hall_building.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Winnipeg%27s_City_Hall_building.JPG/330px-Winnipeg%27s_City_Hall_building.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Winnipeg%27s_City_Hall_building.JPG/440px-Winnipeg%27s_City_Hall_building.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnipeg%27s_City_Hall_building.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winnipeg City Hall is the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_City_Council" title="Winnipeg City Council">seat of municipal government</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Since 1992, the city of Winnipeg has been represented by 15 city councillors and a mayor, both elected every four years.<sup id="cite_ref-munic_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-munic-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> The present mayor, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Bowman_(politician)" title="Brian Bowman (politician)">Brian Bowman</a>, was elected to office in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ce_17-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ce-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The city is a single-tier municipality, governed by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor-council_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor-council government">mayor-council system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ce_17-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ce-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The structure of the municipal government is set by the provincial legislature in the City of Winnipeg Charter Act, which replaced the old <a href="/wiki/City_of_Winnipeg_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="City of Winnipeg Act">City of Winnipeg Act</a> in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-charter_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> The mayor is elected by direct popular vote to serve as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">chief executive</a> of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> At Council meetings, the mayor has one of 16 votes. The City Council is a <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> legislative body, representing geographical <a href="/wiki/Ward_(division)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ward (division)">wards</a> throughout the city.<sup id="cite_ref-charter_202-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In provincial politics, Winnipeg is represented by 31 of the 57 provincial <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Legislative_Assembly" title="Member of the Legislative Assembly">Members of the Legislative Assembly</a> (MLAs). As of 2016, Winnipeg districts are represented by 17 members of the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Conservative_Party_of_Manitoba" title="Progressive Conservative Party of Manitoba">Progressive Conservative Party</a>, 10 by the <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_of_Manitoba" title="New Democratic Party of Manitoba">New Democratic Party</a> (NDP), and 2 by the <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Liberal_Party" title="Manitoba Liberal Party">Liberal Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lesislaturemb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Lesislaturemb.jpg/220px-Lesislaturemb.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Lesislaturemb.jpg/330px-Lesislaturemb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Lesislaturemb.jpg/440px-Lesislaturemb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1530" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lesislaturemb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winnipeg is home to the <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Legislative_Building" title="Manitoba Legislative Building">Manitoba Legislative Building</a>, which houses the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Manitoba" title="Legislative Assembly of Manitoba">Legislative Assembly of Manitoba</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In federal politics, as of 2015 Winnipeg is represented by eight <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_Canada" title="House of Commons of Canada">Members of Parliament</a>: seven <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Canada" title="Liberal Party of Canada">Liberals</a> and one <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_(Canada)" class="mw-redirect" title="New Democratic Party (Canada)">New Democrat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> There are six <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Canada" title="Senate of Canada">Senators</a> representing Manitoba in <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>: three Liberals, two Conservatives, and one Independent.<sup id="cite_ref-senate_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-senate-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law,_government,_and_crime_in_Winnipeg" title="Law, government, and crime in Winnipeg">Law, government, and crime in Winnipeg</a></div>\n<p>From 2007 to 2011, Winnipeg was the "murder capital" of Canada, with the highest per-capita rate of <a href="/wiki/Homicide" title="Homicide">homicides</a>; it fell to second place in 2012, behind <a href="/wiki/Thunder_Bay" title="Thunder Bay">Thunder Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Winnipeg has had the highest <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Canada#Violent_crime_severity_index_by_CMA" title="Crime in Canada">violent crime index</a> since 2009. The robbery rate in 2012 was between 250.1 and 272.9.<sup id="cite_ref-CrimeStat_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrimeStat-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-crimesc_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimesc-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Despite high overall violent crime rates, crime in Winnipeg is mostly concentrated in the inner city, which makes up only 19% of the population<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> but was the site of 86.4% of the city\'s shootings, 66.5% of the robberies, 63.3% of the homicides and 59.5% of the sexual assaults in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-CrimeStat_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrimeStat-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From the early 1990s to the mid-2000s, Winnipeg had a significant auto-theft problem, with the rate peaking at 2,165.0 per 100,000 residents in 2006<sup id="cite_ref-Every_Annual_Crime_Report_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Every_Annual_Crime_Report-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> compared to 487 auto-thefts per 100,000 residents for Canada as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> To combat auto theft, <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Public_Insurance" title="Manitoba Public Insurance">Manitoba Public Insurance</a> established financial incentives for motor vehicle owners to install ignition <a href="/wiki/Immobilizer" class="mw-redirect" title="Immobilizer">immobilizers</a> in their vehicles, and now requires owners of high-risk vehicles to install immobilizers.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> The auto-theft rate has been on a <a href="/wiki/Law,_government,_and_crime_in_Winnipeg#Crime_Rates" title="Law, government, and crime in Winnipeg">constant drop</a> since 2006. Other types of property crime have also decreased, but rates are still fairly high.<sup id="cite_ref-crimesc_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimesc-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-crime12_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crime12-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winnipeg is protected by the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Police_Service" title="Winnipeg Police Service">Winnipeg Police Service</a>, which in 2012 had 1,442 police officers.<sup id="cite_ref-crime12_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crime12-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> In November 2013, the national police union reviewed the Winnipeg Police Force and found high average response times for several categories of calls.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_of_Winnipeg" title="List of schools of Winnipeg">List of schools of Winnipeg</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UManitoba_Administration_Building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/UManitoba_Administration_Building.jpg/220px-UManitoba_Administration_Building.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/UManitoba_Administration_Building.jpg/330px-UManitoba_Administration_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/UManitoba_Administration_Building.jpg/440px-UManitoba_Administration_Building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2006" data-file-height="1489" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UManitoba_Administration_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Located in Winnipeg, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manitoba" title="University of Manitoba">University of Manitoba</a> is the largest post-secondary institution in the province.</div></div></div>\n<p>Winnipeg has seven <a href="/wiki/School_division" title="School division">school divisions</a>: <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_School_Division" title="Winnipeg School Division">Winnipeg School Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._James-Assiniboia_School_Division" title="St. James-Assiniboia School Division">St. James-Assiniboia School Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pembina_Trails_School_Division" title="Pembina Trails School Division">Pembina Trails School Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seven_Oaks_School_Division" title="Seven Oaks School Division">Seven Oaks School Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franco-manitoban_School_Division" title="Franco-manitoban School Division">Division Scolaire Franco-Manitobaine</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_East_Transcona_School_Division" title="River East Transcona School Division">River East Transcona School Division</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Riel_School_Division" title="Louis Riel School Division">Louis Riel School Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Winnipeg also has several religious and secular private schools.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manitoba" title="University of Manitoba">University of Manitoba</a> is the largest university in Manitoba.<sup id="cite_ref-um_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-um-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> It was founded in 1877, making it Western Canada\'s first university.<sup id="cite_ref-um_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-um-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> In a typical year, the university has 24,500 undergraduate students and 4,000 graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Saint-Boniface" title="Universit\xc3\xa9 de Saint-Boniface">Universit\xc3\xa9 de Saint-Boniface</a> is the city\'s only <a href="/wiki/French-language" class="mw-redirect" title="French-language">French-language</a> university.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Winnipeg" title="University of Winnipeg">University of Winnipeg</a> received its charter in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-uw_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uw-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Until 2007, it was an <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate</a> institution that offered some joint graduate studies programs; it now offers independent <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate programs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uw_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uw-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Mennonite_University" title="Canadian Mennonite University">Canadian Mennonite University</a> is a private <a href="/wiki/Mennonite" class="mw-redirect" title="Mennonite">Mennonite</a> undergraduate university established in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winnipeg also has two independent colleges: <a href="/wiki/Red_River_College" title="Red River College">Red River College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Booth_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Booth College">Booth University College</a>. Red River College offers diploma, certificate, and apprenticeship programs and, starting in 2009, began offering some degree programs.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Booth University College is a private Christian <a href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a> university college established in 1982. It offers mostly arts and <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a> training.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Winnipeg" title="Transport in Winnipeg">Transport in Winnipeg</a></div>\n<p>Winnipeg, Manitoba, Canada has had public transit since 1882, starting with <a href="/wiki/Horsecar" title="Horsecar">horse-drawn streetcars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-horse_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horse-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> They were replaced by <a href="/wiki/Electric_tram" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric tram">electric trolley cars</a>. The trolley cars ran from 1892 to 1955, supplemented by motor <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">buses</a> after 1918, and electric <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybuses</a> from 1938 to 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-horse_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horse-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Transit" title="Winnipeg Transit">Winnipeg Transit</a> now runs diesel buses on <a href="/wiki/List_of_Winnipeg_bus_routes" title="List of Winnipeg bus routes">its routes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnipeg_Via_Rail_station_(6327590499).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Winnipeg_Via_Rail_station_%286327590499%29.jpg/220px-Winnipeg_Via_Rail_station_%286327590499%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Winnipeg_Via_Rail_station_%286327590499%29.jpg/330px-Winnipeg_Via_Rail_station_%286327590499%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Winnipeg_Via_Rail_station_%286327590499%29.jpg/440px-Winnipeg_Via_Rail_station_%286327590499%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnipeg_Via_Rail_station_(6327590499).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Winnipeg)" title="Union Station (Winnipeg)">Union Station</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Intercity_rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Intercity rail">inter-city</a> <a href="/wiki/Railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway station">railway station</a> for the city.</div></div></div>\n<p>Winnipeg is a railway hub and is served by <a href="/wiki/Via_Rail" title="Via Rail">Via Rail</a> at <a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Winnipeg)" title="Union Station (Winnipeg)">Union Station</a> for passenger rail, and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_National_Railway" title="Canadian National Railway">Canadian National Railway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Pacific_Railway" title="Canadian Pacific Railway">Canadian Pacific Railway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burlington_Northern_Santa_Fe_Manitoba" title="Burlington Northern Santa Fe Manitoba">Burlington Northern Santa Fe Manitoba</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Central_Manitoba_Railway" title="Central Manitoba Railway">Central Manitoba Railway</a> for <a href="/wiki/Rail_freight_transport" title="Rail freight transport">freight rail</a>. It is the only major city between Vancouver and <a href="/wiki/Thunder_Bay" title="Thunder Bay">Thunder Bay</a> with direct US connections by rail.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winnipeg, Manitoba, Canada is the largest and best connected city within Manitoba, and has highways leading in all directions from the city. To the south, Winnipeg is connected to the United States via <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Highway_75" title="Manitoba Highway 75">Provincial Trunk Highway 75 (PTH 75)</a> (a continuation of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_29" title="Interstate 29">I-29</a> and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_75" title="U.S. Route 75">US 75</a>, known as Pembina Highway or <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Route_42" title="Winnipeg Route 42">Route 42</a> within Winnipeg). The highway runs 107&#160;km (66&#160;mi) to <a href="/wiki/Emerson,_Manitoba" title="Emerson, Manitoba">Emerson, Manitoba</a>, and is the busiest <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Canada\xe2\x80\x93United States border">Canada\xe2\x80\x93United States border</a> crossing on the Prairies.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> The four-lane <a href="/wiki/Perimeter_Highway_(Winnipeg)" title="Perimeter Highway (Winnipeg)">Perimeter Highway</a>, built in 1969, serves as a <a href="/wiki/Beltway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beltway">Ring Road</a>, with <a href="/wiki/At-grade_intersection" class="mw-redirect" title="At-grade intersection">at-grade intersections</a> and a few <a href="/wiki/Interchange_(road)" title="Interchange (road)">interchanges</a>. It allows travellers on the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Canada_Highway" title="Trans-Canada Highway">Trans-Canada Highway</a> to bypass the city. A recent study cited dangerous intersections and low efficiency as its primary shortfalls.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Trans-Canada_Highway" title="Trans-Canada Highway">Trans-Canada Highway</a> runs east to west through the city (city route), or circles around the city on the Perimeter Highway (beltway). Some of the city\'s major arterial roads include <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Route_80" title="Winnipeg Route 80">Route 80 (Waverley St.)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Route_155" title="Winnipeg Route 155">Route 155 (McGillivray Blvd)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Route_165" title="Winnipeg Route 165">Route 165 (Bishop Grandin Blvd.)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Route_17" title="Winnipeg Route 17">Route 17 (Chief Peguis Trail)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Route_90" title="Winnipeg Route 90">Route 90 (Brookside Blvd., Oak Point Hwy., King Edward St., Century St., Kenaston Blvd.)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnipeg_International_Airport_arrivals_hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Winnipeg_International_Airport_arrivals_hall.jpg/220px-Winnipeg_International_Airport_arrivals_hall.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Winnipeg_International_Airport_arrivals_hall.jpg/330px-Winnipeg_International_Airport_arrivals_hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Winnipeg_International_Airport_arrivals_hall.jpg/440px-Winnipeg_International_Airport_arrivals_hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2518" data-file-height="1880" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnipeg_International_Airport_arrivals_hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_James_Armstrong_Richardson_International_Airport" title="Winnipeg James Armstrong Richardson International Airport">Winnipeg James Armstrong Richardson International Airport</a> is the only commercial <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in the province.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_James_Armstrong_Richardson_International_Airport" title="Winnipeg James Armstrong Richardson International Airport">Winnipeg James Armstrong Richardson International Airport</a> completed a $585-million redevelopment in October 2011. The development brought a new terminal, a four-level parking facility, and other infrastructure improvements.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Bus_Terminal" title="Winnipeg Bus Terminal">Winnipeg Bus Terminal</a>, at Winnipeg International Airport, offers domestic and international service by <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Canada" title="Greyhound Canada">Greyhound Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grey_Goose_Bus_Lines" title="Grey Goose Bus Lines">Grey Goose Bus Lines</a>, Winnipeg Shuttle Service and Brandon Air Shuttle.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Approximately 20,000 acres (81&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of land to the north and west of the airport has been designated as an <a href="/wiki/Inland_port" title="Inland port">inland port</a>, <a href="/wiki/CentrePort_Canada" title="CentrePort Canada">CentrePort Canada</a>, and is Canada\'s first <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Trade_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Trade Zone">Foreign Trade Zone</a>. It is a private sector initiative to develop the infrastructure for Manitoba\'s trucking, air, rail and sea industries.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, construction began on a $212-million four-lane freeway to connect CentrePort with the Perimeter Highway.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Named CentrePort Canada Way, it opened in November 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several taxi companies serve Winnipeg, the largest being Unicity, Duffy\'s Taxi and Spring Taxi. Fifty percent of Winnipeg residents use a taxi at least once during the year.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Ride sharing was legalized in March 2018 and several services including TappCar and Cowboy Taxi operate in Winnipeg.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Cycling is popular in Winnipeg, and there are many bicycle trails and lanes around the city. Winnipeg holds an annual <a href="/wiki/Bike-to-Work_Day" title="Bike-to-Work Day">Bike-to-Work Day</a><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cyclovia" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclovia">Cyclovia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> and bicycle commuters may be seen year-round, even in the winter. Active living infrastructure in Winnipeg encourages bicycling through the inclusion of <a href="/wiki/Bike_lanes" class="mw-redirect" title="Bike lanes">bike lanes</a><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Shared_lane_marking" title="Shared lane marking">sharrows</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_centres_and_hospitals">Medical centres and hospitals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Medical centres and hospitals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Manitoba" title="List of hospitals in Manitoba">List of hospitals in Manitoba</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Boniface_Hospital,_Winnipeg_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/St._Boniface_Hospital%2C_Winnipeg_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-St._Boniface_Hospital%2C_Winnipeg_-_panoramio.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/St._Boniface_Hospital%2C_Winnipeg_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-St._Boniface_Hospital%2C_Winnipeg_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/St._Boniface_Hospital%2C_Winnipeg_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-St._Boniface_Hospital%2C_Winnipeg_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1151" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Boniface_Hospital,_Winnipeg_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St._Boniface_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Boniface Hospital">St. Boniface Hospital</a> is one of several medical centres located in the city.</div></div></div>\n<p>Winnipeg\'s major hospitals include <a href="/wiki/Health_Sciences_Centre_(Winnipeg)" title="Health Sciences Centre (Winnipeg)">Health Sciences Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concordia_Hospital" title="Concordia Hospital">Concordia Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deer_Lodge_Centre" title="Deer Lodge Centre">Deer Lodge Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grace_Hospital_(Winnipeg)" title="Grace Hospital (Winnipeg)">Grace Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Misericordia_Health_Centre" title="Misericordia Health Centre">Misericordia Health Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riverview_Health_Centre" title="Riverview Health Centre">Riverview Health Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Boniface_General_Hospital_(Winnipeg)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Boniface General Hospital (Winnipeg)">Saint Boniface General Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seven_Oaks_General_Hospital" title="Seven Oaks General Hospital">Seven Oaks General Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_General_Hospital_(Winnipeg)" title="Victoria General Hospital (Winnipeg)">Victoria General Hospital</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Children%27s_Hospital_of_Winnipeg" title="The Children&#39;s Hospital of Winnipeg">The Children\'s Hospital of Winnipeg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Microbiology_Laboratory" title="National Microbiology Laboratory">National Microbiology Laboratory</a> in Winnipeg is one of only a handful of <a href="/wiki/Biosafety_level" title="Biosafety level">biosafety level</a> 4 microbiology laboratories in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> The NML houses laboratories of the Public Health Agency of Canada (PHAC) and the Canadian Food Inspection Agency, in the National Centre for Foreign Animal Disease collocated in the same facility. Research facilities are also operated through hospitals and private biotechnology companies in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Water and sewage services are provided by the city.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> The city draws its water via an <a href="/wiki/Greater_Winnipeg_Water_District_aqueduct" title="Greater Winnipeg Water District aqueduct">aqueduct</a> from <a href="/wiki/Shoal_Lake_(Kenora_District,_Ontario)" title="Shoal Lake (Kenora District, Ontario)">Shoal Lake</a>, treating and <a href="/wiki/Water_fluoridation" title="Water fluoridation">fluoridating</a> it at the Deacon Reservoir just outside the city prior to pumping it into the Winnipeg system.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s system has over 2,500 kilometres (1,600&#160;mi) of underground water mains, which are subject to breakage during extreme weather conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">Electricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> are provided by <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Hydro" title="Manitoba Hydro">Manitoba Hydro</a>, a provincial <a href="/wiki/Crown_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown corporation">crown corporation</a> headquartered in the city; it uses primarily <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric">hydroelectric</a> power.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> The primary telecommunications carrier is <a href="/wiki/Manitoba_Telecom_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Manitoba Telecom Services">MTS</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> although other corporations offer telephone, cellular, television and internet services.\n</p><p>Winnipeg contracts out several services to private companies, including garbage and recycling collection and street plowing and snow removal. This practice represents a significant budget expenditure and is more expansive than in comparable communities. The services have faced numerous complaints from residents in 2013\xe2\x80\x9314 about missed service.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/CFB_Winnipeg" title="CFB Winnipeg">CFB Winnipeg</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CFB_Winnipeg_17_Wing_sign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/CFB_Winnipeg_17_Wing_sign.jpg/220px-CFB_Winnipeg_17_Wing_sign.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/CFB_Winnipeg_17_Wing_sign.jpg/330px-CFB_Winnipeg_17_Wing_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/CFB_Winnipeg_17_Wing_sign.jpg/440px-CFB_Winnipeg_17_Wing_sign.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CFB_Winnipeg_17_Wing_sign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance to <a href="/wiki/CFB_Winnipeg" title="CFB Winnipeg">CFB Winnipeg</a>. CFB Winnipeg is the home garrison for a number of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Force" title="Royal Canadian Air Force">Royal Canadian Air Force</a> units.</div></div></div> \n<p><a href="/wiki/CFB_Winnipeg" title="CFB Winnipeg">Canadian Forces Base Winnipeg</a>, co-located at the <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_James_Armstrong_Richardson_International_Airport" title="Winnipeg James Armstrong Richardson International Airport">airport</a>, is home to many flight operations support divisions and several training schools. It is also the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/1_Canadian_Air_Division" title="1 Canadian Air Division">1 Canadian Air Division</a> and the Canadian <a href="/wiki/North_American_Aerospace_Defense_Command" title="North American Aerospace Defense Command">North American Aerospace Defense Command</a> (NORAD) Region,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> as well as the home base of 17 Wing of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian Forces">Canadian Forces</a>. The Wing comprises three squadrons and six schools; it also provides support to the Central Flying School.<sup id="cite_ref-17_Wing_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17_Wing-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Excluding the three levels of government, 17 Wing is the fourth largest employer in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> The Wing supports 113 units, stretching from <a href="/wiki/Thunder_Bay" title="Thunder Bay">Thunder Bay</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">Saskatchewan</a>&#8211;<a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> border, and from the <a href="/wiki/49th_parallel_north" title="49th parallel north">49th parallel</a> to the high <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17_Wing_259-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17_Wing-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> 17 Wing also acts as a deployed operating base for <a href="/wiki/CF-18_Hornet" class="mw-redirect" title="CF-18 Hornet">CF-18 Hornet</a> <a href="/wiki/Ground-attack_aircraft" class="mw-redirect" title="Ground-attack aircraft">fighter-bombers</a> assigned to the Canadian NORAD Region.<sup id="cite_ref-17_Wing_259-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17_Wing-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are two squadrons based in the city. The <a href="/wiki/No._402_Squadron_RCAF" class="mw-redirect" title="No. 402 Squadron RCAF">402 "City of Winnipeg" Squadron</a> flies the Canadian-designed and produced de Havilland <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Canada_Dash_8" class="mw-redirect" title="De Havilland Canada Dash 8">CT-142 Dash 8</a> navigation trainer.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/435_Transport_and_Rescue_Squadron" title="435 Transport and Rescue Squadron">435 "Chinthe" Transport and Rescue Squadron</a> flies the Lockheed <a href="/wiki/C-130_Hercules" class="mw-redirect" title="C-130 Hercules">CC-130 Hercules</a> in airlift <a href="/wiki/Search_and_rescue" title="Search and rescue">search and rescue</a> roles.<sup id="cite_ref-chinte_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinte-262">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> In addition, 435 Squadron is the only <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Force" title="Royal Canadian Air Force">Royal Canadian Air Force</a> squadron equipped and trained to conduct tactical <a href="/wiki/Aerial_refueling" title="Aerial refueling">air-to-air refueling</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">fighter aircraft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chinte_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinte-262">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For many years, Winnipeg was the home of the Second Battalion of <a href="/wiki/Princess_Patricia%27s_Canadian_Light_Infantry" title="Princess Patricia&#39;s Canadian Light Infantry">Princess Patricia\'s Canadian Light Infantry</a>. Initially, the battalion was based at the Fort Osborne Barracks, now the location of the Rady Jewish Community Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> They eventually moved to the Kapyong Barracks between <a href="/wiki/River_Heights,_Winnipeg" title="River Heights, Winnipeg">River Heights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuxedo,_Winnipeg" title="Tuxedo, Winnipeg">Tuxedo</a>. Since 2004, the battalion has operated out of <a href="/wiki/CFB_Shilo" title="CFB Shilo">CFB Shilo</a> near <a href="/wiki/Brandon,_Manitoba" title="Brandon, Manitoba">Brandon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Winnipeg" title="List of people from Winnipeg">List of people from Winnipeg</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Winnipeg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a
